The 20th Anniversary of the Ta Lu Pao 146

A New Atmosphere After the Return of the Chinese

A Huge Commemorative Special Issue is Published

Shanghai, by virtue of its commercial, political, historical, and geographical relationships, is the center of the domestic news industry. In recent years, the press has undergone many changes, and the most noteworthy of these is the acquisition of the Ta Lu Pao by the Chinese.

Shanghai has three English morning newspapers that are equally famous. The Ta Lu Pao is one of them. The Ta Lu Pao was founded in 1911, exactly 20 years ago. At that time, the revolutionary tide was surging, and the international atmosphere was somewhat anxious. President Sun, Mr. Wu Tingfang, Mr. Tang Shaoyi, etc., pooled funds and entrusted Mr. Miller, an American, to run the newspaper to correct international perceptions. This was the beginning of the Ta Lu Pao. Later, the world changed, and President Sun and others had no time to take care of it, so it fell into American hands. The hosts were repeatedly replaced, but because it was registered in the United States, everyone knew that it was an organ of the Americans. Last October, it was acquired by people from the Chinese press. Since then, the Ta Lu Pao has become the only English Chinese newspaper in Shanghai.

Since October, the Ta Lu Pao has made considerable progress. This is because the managers are experts in the field (the chief editor is Mr. Dong Xianguang, who has long been respected in the press and who founded the Tianjin Yong Bao), and the approach to material is in line with its nature and position. There are two obvious aspects: (1) In terms of business, sales and advertising have both increased sharply. Sales have increased by more than double, and advertising has increased by one-third. (2) In terms of editing, in addition to continuing to pay attention to international news, Sino-foreign trade, literature and art, technology, and film, in order to maintain its original foreign readers and the face of an English newspaper, it has made every effort to seek detailed and accurate information on Chinese political news, social problems, construction plans, and the opinions of Chinese businessmen. (It is also able to disclose Chinese news one day earlier than foreign newspapers.) It has corrected the flaws of foreign newspapers that are sensational, superficial, and biased. Although its attitude in its commentary is completely based on the interests of China, it has been able to express the spirit of advocating fairness because it has tried to avoid narrowness and to be sincere. These few things meet the practical needs of foreigners, because most legitimate foreigners are in China to engage in industry and commerce, so what they seek to know is the truth and true intentions of China, and they are not happy to hear rumors and strange theories that are unfavorable to China. Therefore, in the past, the Ta Lu Pao, because of its national relationship, was best able to absorb American expatriates as readers, but after the reorganization, it has been universally noticed and trusted by expatriate merchants from various countries and their home countries. This is the main reason for the success of the past October.

After the Chinese obtained this Ta Lu Pao, of course, they regarded external publicity for the country as their duty, and the Chinese business community in Shanghai has gradually understood the necessity of a mouthpiece for the outside world, so they have been able to make considerable use of the Ta Lu Pao and regard it as a medium for promoting Sino-foreign trade. Usually, they pay close attention to the Ta Lu Pao, and when necessary, they use the Ta Lu Pao's advertisements and chronicles to avoid harm and seek benefits, and to promote their business. The Ta Lu Pao has benefited greatly from these circumstances, which is due to its efforts and not to chance. It is reported that the Ta Lu Pao is now planning a vigorous advancement plan, aiming to fulfill its foreign mission to the Chinese government and the public, that is, to make practical contributions in the political, diplomatic, economic, commercial, and even cultural and artistic fields.

August 29th of this year is the 20th anniversary of the founding of the Ta Lu Pao, and a special issue of 100 large pages will be published on September 15th. Chairman Chiang, Vice Commander Zhang, Foreign Minister Wang, Industry Minister Kong, Transportation Minister Wang, Railway Minister Lian, Health Minister Liu, Shanghai Mayor Zhang, Foreign Ministry Information Department Chief Diao, China Bank Mr. Zhang Gongquan, Zhejiang Industrial Bank Mr. Li Xinsun, Chinese press celebrities Shi Liangcai, Zhang Zhuping, Pan Gongbi, Wang Yingbin, Ge Gongzhen, Wang Boqi, Lin Zhenbin, and other gentlemen, and other Chinese and foreign celebrities, either wrote congratulatory messages or contributed their great works, which are dazzling and beautiful. Chairman Chiang said that the Ta Lu Pao was founded at the same time as the Republic of China and has a history of 20 years. In his congratulatory message, he paid special attention to it. The essays by Chinese and foreign celebrities are mostly about China's new construction in the past 20 years, and none of them are worthless. Their value is self-evident. It is reported that a total of 30,000 copies of the special issue will be printed and distributed all over the world. This kind of commemoration is a new record for Western newspapers in Shanghai. The colleagues of the Ta Lu Pao have been preparing for this event for several months, so it is appropriate that they have achieved this result.

In addition to publishing a special issue to commemorate its 20th anniversary, the Ta Lu Pao has also formulated preferential measures for subscribers in order to popularize it. Ordinary subscribers can receive a 20% discount on the annual price of 24 yuan, and student subscribers will receive even more preferential treatment. The annual special price of 18 yuan can be further discounted by 5%. This is a great opportunity for Chinese people to read English newspapers. Do not neglect it. The staff serving at the Ta Lu Pao are of seven nationalities, namely Chinese, English, American, French, Portuguese, Japanese, and Korean. Moreover, there are not only men, but also many women. This shows the breadth of its talent recruitment, which is not limited by national boundaries and cannot be achieved by other newspapers. (September 14)

Measures for Reducing Prices of Grain Transported for Sale at Government-Regulated Prices 150

The Municipal Government Orders the Social Affairs Bureau to Circulate the Information

The Municipal Government received an order from the Executive Yuan regarding measures to reduce prices of grain transported for sale at government-regulated prices, and yesterday instructed the Social Affairs Bureau to circulate the information. The measures are as follows: (1) The freight rates for all grain transported to disaster areas for sale at government-regulated prices on state-owned railways will be reduced by 50%. (2) Local governments, charitable organizations, and merchants in disaster areas requesting transportation of grain for sale at government-regulated prices must submit applications to the provincial and municipal governments of each province, stating the type and quantity of grain, the route, and the origin and destination stations. The applications will then be forwarded to the Ministry of Railways, which will instruct the railway administrations to provide transportation according to the reduced price measures. (3) Grain transported from the provinces of Guandong (Manchuria) and the Yellow River basin to disaster areas will be limited to millet, Indian millet, corn, flour, sweet potatoes, wheat flour, buckwheat flour, soybeans, broad beans, and sorghum. (4) Grain transported from the provinces of the Yangtze and Pearl River basins to disaster areas will be limited to coarse rice. (5) The following stations are temporarily designated as terminal stations for transporting grain for sale at government-regulated prices: Xinyang, Huayuan, Xiaogan, and Hankou on the Peiping-Hankow Railway; Xuzhou, Bengbu, and Pukou on the Tianjin-Pukou Railway; Xuzhou and Dapu on the Longhai Railway; all stations on the Hunan-Hubei Railway; and all stations on the Nanxun Railway. The Ministry of Railways may add to or reduce the aforementioned railways and reduced-price terminal stations at any time. (6) These measures will be in effect for a period of six months.

The Loans Borrowed by the Jiangsu Provincial Government for Dike Construction Have Been Remitted 151

The Jiangsu Provincial Government authorities, due to the breaches in the dikes and the disasters in Gaoyou and Shaobo, urgently needed funds to address the aftermath. Local News II

Kidnappers Run Rampant, Entering Homes to Abduct Victims 158

Pu Wenting Arrives in Shanghai from Wuxi

Playing Mahjong at the Qi Family's Residence

Three Kidnappers Arrive for a "Visit"

After Meeting, They Forcibly Abduct Him

At approximately 8:00 p.m. last night, a bizarre kidnapping occurred in Simingli, Foch Road, in the French Concession. The criminals boldly entered the house and openly abducted the victim, setting a new record in Shanghai's kidnapping cases. This further demonstrates the rampant nature of kidnappers. The details are as follows:

▲ A woman surnamed Wang rented a house in the French Concession, west of Foch Road, in a lane called Chenghecun. Recently, due to a change of residence and employment at the Siming Bank, a new-style building was rebuilt, and the lane was renamed Simingli. Two weeks ago, a woman claiming to be Wang rented a shikumen house at No. 19 in the lane. Wang herself occupied the ground floor, while the second floor was sublet to another woman who also happened to be surnamed Wang.

▲ Accompanying Guest Plays Mahjong The day before yesterday (the 12th), a relative from Wuxi named Pu Wenting came to Wang's house. Pu, 58 years old, worked at the Fuxin Flour Mill in Wuxi. After arriving in Shanghai, he stayed at Wang's residence. Yesterday afternoon, Wang and the Wang woman from upstairs invited two acquaintances, young ladies, to accompany Pu in playing mahjong for entertainment. Unexpectedly, a sudden incident occurred around 8:00 p.m.

▲ Three Men Visit Mr. Pu As Pu and the three women were deeply engrossed in their mahjong game, Fan Ma, a female servant at Wang's house, was preparing dinner in the kitchen. Suddenly, she heard someone knocking on the back door with their fingers. When the servant asked who it was, a voice outside the door replied, "Visiting Mr. Pu." The servant opened the door and saw three men wearing long gowns, entering in single file, with a calm demeanor, resembling ruffians. The servant told the guests to wait a moment and stretched her neck to call for Mr. Pu upstairs.

▲ Two Men Approach the Stairs As the three men entered, the servant asked them why they were visiting Mr. Pu. One of them replied that they were in the flour business and had a business matter to discuss. The servant, seeing them as Pu's friends, told them to wait downstairs while she called Pu down. At this time, two of the men approached both sides of the stairs. One of them pulled his clothes and sat down on the long bench near the back door, waiting for the arrival of their "god of wealth."

▲ Pistols Appear Simultaneously Upon hearing the call, Pu did not hesitate and immediately got up, taking large steps downstairs and repeatedly asking, "Who is it?" As Pu stepped down to the lowest step, two men suddenly emerged, blocking the stairs. When Pu turned around to get a good look, two black and shiny pistols were already pressed against his left and right waist, as if bodyguards were escorting a high-ranking official. They surged out of the back door.

▲ Driven Away in a Car At the same time, the man sitting on the bench, witnessing the victim being captured, rushed out the back door, jumped into a car, and started the engine. In an instant, the two men had forced Pu into the car. With a "whirring" sound, the car sped out of the lane towards the east. At this time, Fan the servant woke up as if from a dream and reported the incident upstairs. The three women were extremely shocked upon hearing the news. When they rushed to the entrance of the lane to report to the Chinese constable guarding the entrance, the kidnappers were already long gone.

▲ The Woman's Evasive Answers The police station was also notified at the same time, and detectives went to investigate. Reporters from this newspaper also arrived one after another. According to the Wang woman, the sublessor, her husband's name is Wang Junlai. When asked what his current occupation was, she looked embarrassed, and after hesitating for a long time, replied that he (referring to her husband) had not returned for several years. He had once worked in the military. "Gentlemen (referring to the reporters), just write whatever you want," she said, with an uneasy and flustered attitude and an unusually vague tone.

▲ Rumors Among Passersby A reporter also privately inquired with people in the same building. It was reported that the woman upstairs was actually Pu's concubine, and the so-called sublessor, Mrs. Wang, was also very intimate with Pu. The secrets within were not something that outsiders could understand even a fraction of. As for the car used by the kidnappers, it was waiting directly behind No. 19, about dozens of yards away from the entrance of the lane. Since there were many residents in the lane who owned or hired cars, the Chinese constable guarding the entrance did not pay much attention. It was truly unexpected that the kidnappers would dare to openly drive a car into the lane and enter the house to abduct the victim. According to one or two passersby, they had indeed seen a car speeding out of the lane a moment ago. It was a black-plated private car. The sublessor, Mrs. Wang, has urgently telegraphed Pu's eldest son, Pu Yongda, in Wuxi, to come to Shanghai immediately to take charge of the situation.

Two Tides in Shanghai in One Day 159

Huangpu River Tides Overflowing the Banks

Since this summer and autumn, the tides have risen greatly, causing severe flooding in various provinces, with waters not receding for several days or even weeks. The severity of the disasters is unprecedented. However, the tides in Shanghai recently have undergone special changes, with two tides occurring in one day, which can also be described as a new unprecedented record. Due to rumors of the tide landing on the 25th of last month, causing public anxiety, the maximum height of the recent high tides is also a matter of great concern to the general public. According to staff at the Wusong Fort Taiwan Cheqi (flag station), the tide rises and falls twice every day and night, which is known to everyone. However, the recent oddity of the tides is unprecedented. According to their work experience, whenever the tide first rises, the rising water (i.e., the bamboo-made black ball) is hoisted to indicate navigation to ships. Traditionally, it takes four hours from the time the ball is hoisted for the tide to recede. Unexpectedly, recently, there have been instances where the tide receded in only three hours, and even more so where the tide rose again before the water had fallen for two hours. This kind of unusual situation has occurred several times at the end of last month and the beginning of this month. The unpredictable tides are dangerous for sailing ships, and they also affect the accuracy of reports on the work and accounting records of the staff, causing great difficulties in their duties. However, the tides of the previous two days (i.e., the first day of the lunar calendar) were not high. The second day was slightly higher, with the daytime tide rising to 38 feet and the nighttime tide being five inches higher. Yesterday (i.e., the third day), the daytime tide was 38 feet 1 inch, and it is feared that the nighttime tide will be higher. Because the previous day was a strong southerly wind blowing eastward, yesterday morning the south wind turned westward, and in the afternoon it turned into a northeast wind, but it was not strong. Therefore, although the nighttime tide is predicted to be large, it is not expected to exceed 40 feet, and there should be no danger.

Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 p.m., when the tide came in, the force was very strong, causing the Huangpu River to be unable to hold the volume of water, overflowing the banks. The Bund Park and areas along the Huangpu River bank, South Sichuan Road, and Fuzhou Road were flooded with about six inches of water due to the low terrain. Some ignorant and foolish people passing by mistakenly believed that Shanghai would become a second Hankou, and were in a state of panic. The tide receded after about an hour.

Three Robbers Rob a Child in the Middle of the Night, Killing One and Capturing One 160

They Encountered Patrol Detectives

Only One of the Three Robbers Escaped

Chen Shimin, 25 years old, a native of Nanjing and an employee of the Datong Apartment on Avenue Foch, lived in the Yongyuli at the intersection of Rue Belles and Ximen Road. At 3:15 a.m. yesterday morning, he finished his work and was riding home in a rickshaw. While traveling along Rue Belles near the intersection of Rue Vouillemont, three robbers suddenly rushed out, blocked the road, and threatened him with a fake pistol. They robbed him of a gold watch and a wallet containing 13 yuan. The robbers fled north with their loot. The victim, Chen Shimin, chased after them, shouting for help. One robber fled into the Fuzhifang on Rue Belles. Detectives and inspectors of a special squad, Jin Jiulin, detective Li Yaolong, assistant detectives Xu Yumin, Mao Jingen, and Zhang Ziying, and Chinese constable No. 648 and Vietnamese constable No. 309, who were on patrol, heard the cries and rushed to the scene. They captured one of the robbers and confiscated the iron fake pistol and the original stolen wallet, and took him to the police station. Another robber fled to the intersection of Rue Belles and Avenue Dubail and was spotted by Vietnamese constable No. 141, who ordered him to stop. When he refused to listen, the constable drew his gun and fired, hitting him in the chest. He fell to the ground and died instantly. The other robber escaped without a trace. According to the captured robber, his name is Jiang Renyong, 29 years old, a native of Tongzhou. The robber who escaped is named Xiao San, and the robber who was shot dead is named Si Lunzi, around 30 years old, a native of Tongzhou. He confessed to committing the robbery with the others. The police chief ordered that he be detained. Detectives were sent to take the robber's body to the Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Home for examination. At 10:00 a.m., the police station reported the incident to the court for investigation. Judge Luo Renji and Prosecutor Lou Kongxian took their seats in the criminal court for interrogation. The victim described the robbery. When questioned, Jiang confessed to committing the robbery with Xiao San and Si Lunzi, who was shot dead. Because Vietnamese constable No. 141 was required to testify at the examination of the body and had not yet arrived, Judge Luo ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody and scheduled a continued interrogation. Later, at 10:30 a.m., Prosecutor Ding Shikui, along with clerk Peng, medical examiner Hun Ligong, arrived at the site. After examining the robber's body, they took their seats and heard the police's report on the incident. They also stated that the body had no family members. Vietnamese constable No. 141, Jin Huangfang (transliteration), stated that he heard the cries of a robber, ordered him to stop, and fired his gun, resulting in his death. After verifying the testimony, Ding ruled that the deceased, Si Lunzi, died from gunshot wounds sustained during his life. The body was taken to the Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Home for storage.

Japanese Fishing Boat Republic Maru Capsized in Hurricane 161

Only One Sailor Was Rescued

The Japanese Nagasaki Minamimatsuho fishing boat Republic Maru intended to fish in Chinese waters, but shortly after setting sail, it was overturned by a hurricane, drowning eleven people. Yesterday, the Japanese ship Ikoma Maru rescued a Japanese man named Fujiya, who described his experience of drifting at sea and sinking to the bottom of the sea twice. The details are as follows:

▲ Encountered a Large Storm The Nippon Yusen Kaisha's Ikoma Maru set sail from Moji on the afternoon of the 11th and arrived near the Tsushima Strait the next morning. A large storm occurred, with a hurricane and raging waves coming from the southeast. Fortunately, the shipowner Iwashita struggled to bring the ship closer to the strait, avoiding disaster. It was originally scheduled to arrive on the 13th, but it was delayed until yesterday. The passengers on board were all greatly frightened.

▲ The Republic Fishing Boat Was Destroyed and Sunk The fishing boat Republic Maru, carrying twelve sailors, departed from Nagazaki on the 10th. At 11:00 p.m. that night, seventy nautical miles outside Nagasaki, it encountered a large storm. The fishing boat was unable to avoid it. The first large wave struck, sweeping six fishermen and sailors overboard. As they were about to throw life buoys to rescue them, the first large wave came again. The ship was broken by a wave and immediately sank. The six people who remained on board also fell into the sea.

▲ Only One Passenger Survived After the twelve people on board fell into the sea, they were all separated. As the storm continued, the waves scattered the sailors, such as Zhang Yuanying, Lin Liangjie, Shimoda Akira, Ito, and others, were never seen again. Even their bodies were not found. It is thought that they all drowned. The chief sailor Fujiya, after falling into the sea, was washed to the bottom of the sea by a large wave. Fortunately, he knew how to swim and managed to resurface, but he sank to the bottom of the sea again. After resurfacing again, he managed to grab a piece of broken wood from the ship, only four feet long. Fujiya held on tightly and allowed it to drift with the waves for ten hours.

▲ Rescued and Brought to Shanghai The Japanese man was floating up and down and drifted to the vicinity of Tsushima Island at 8:23 a.m. on the 12th. Fujiya thought he was certain to die. At this time, the wind subsided slightly. He looked up and saw the Ikoma Maru ship sheltering from the wind. Fujiya shouted for help, which was heard by the crew of the Ikoma Maru. The shipowner Iwashita ordered a lifeboat to be lowered into the sea to rescue him. However, the lifeboat was broken by the waves as soon as it entered the sea. They then threw a life preserver into the sea and managed to rescue the Japanese man. After boarding the ship, they changed his wet clothes and gave him food and drink, and brought him to Shanghai.

▲ Handed Over to the Consulate Yesterday, the Ikoma Maru arrived in Shanghai, and Fujiya also came to Shanghai. According to him, he floated in the sea for ten hours, with nine deaths and one survival. The other eleven people on board had already drowned. Yesterday, the Nippon Yusen Kaisha sent Fujiya to the Japanese Consulate in this city, and then the Japanese Consulate sent the Japanese man back to his country.

Tragic Incident of Robbers Killing a Child on the Station Branch Road 162

An Old Woman Upstairs Shouted

The Robbers Fired in Anger

The Bullet Pierced the Girl's Front and Back of the Head

The Mother, Mrs. Kong Zhang, Was Shot in the Arm

Kong Xueyuan, a locomotive driver on the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Southern Railway Station, lived at No. 109 Station Branch Road and had some savings, which attracted the attention of robbers. Around 7:00 p.m. the day before yesterday (13th), Kong was having tea at a tiger stove across the street. Unexpectedly, two robbers wearing black raincoats and rain hats entered the house and asked Kong's wife, Mrs. Kong Zhang, if Old Kong was at home. Mrs. Kong, holding her two-year-old daughter, Mao Tou, walked out of the room and said that her husband was at the tiger stove across the street and that she would go call him. The robbers said that was not necessary, and told her to quickly hand over her money. As they spoke, they took out a gun. Mrs. Kong said that there was no money at home, and even if they pawned their clothes, they would not be worth the demand. While they were threatening her, Kong's nine-year-old child saw this and started crying loudly, running outside. The robbers saw this and dragged the child inside. The robbers, seeing that things had gone wrong, were about to leave when an old woman living upstairs shouted at Mrs. Kong to quickly call Kong Xuegui from outside. The robbers became angry and in a moment of desperation fired the gun. The bullet struck the two-year-old child Mao Tou's head, entering from the front of the head and exiting from the back. The force of the bullet was so great that after passing through, it also struck Mrs. Kong Zhang's right arm. Mother and daughter were both injured and fell to the ground. The robbers then fled in a panic. After Kong Xuegui learned of this, he rushed home and saw his wife and daughter lying in a pool of blood. He immediately sent them to the Shanghai Hospital for treatment. The police station of the Second District Police Department was nearby. By the time the police arrived, the robbers were long gone. After questioning those involved and reporting to the Second District, which then reported to the Public Security Bureau for investigation, Mrs. Kong Zhang and Kong Mao Tou were sent to the hospital. Mrs. Kong Zhang's injuries were not life-threatening, but Mao Tou died from her brain injury at 4:00 a.m. yesterday. Her body was brought home by Kong and reported to the police station, which ordered Zhang Hongxun, the local head of the twelfth tu of the fang, to report to the local court. Prosecutor Wu Shixin, along with clerk Qian Yinpei and inspector Xuan Zhiming, arrived at the scene to examine the body, confirming that she died from the injury. They ordered the body to be prepared for burial. They then went to the Shanghai Hospital to examine Mrs. Kong Zhang's injuries and filled out an autopsy report, ordering the arrest of the murderers.

More Than a Dozen Places Were Raided

Favalier Personally Led the Raid

According to the Continental Daily News, French Concession Director Favalier personally led detectives to raid more than a dozen gambling dens on Saturday morning. A Briton Fraudulently Obtains Goods 164

Signing Dud Checks

Using the Goods to Obtain Money

According to the Ta Mei Wan Pao (Shanghai Evening Post & Mercury), an Englishman named Lushton, posing as an employee of a life insurance company, purchased two cigar boxes and a pair of cufflink chains worth 109 yuan on credit from the Hongchang Company on Nanjing Road. He signed two vouchers promising to pay the amount at a later date. He then pawned the goods and used the money. When the payment was not made, Hongchang sued the police station, requesting the British Police Court to issue a warrant for his arrest. The goods were recovered from a pawnshop. He was brought to the British Public Concession Court for trial today (14th). The defendant admitted to posing as an employee of an insurance company, but denied defrauding for the goods. The Western detective who arrested Lushton and a representative from Hongchang testified to everything. Because another witness had not yet arrived, the hearing was adjourned to a later date.

August Consumption and Value of Aquatic Products in This City 165

Published by the Municipal Fisheries Guidance Institute

August is the typhoon season. Most Chinese fishing boats, both old and new, take this opportunity to repair their vessels, which is called the "slack fishing" period. Therefore, the catch is very small. On the one hand, the weather is hot, and many people abstain from meat, causing the market to be sluggish. According to statistics, this month the city consumed a total of 23,582 "dan" of fresh and frozen fish (excluding 7,530 "dan" of freshwater fish), worth 437,263 yuan. The marine products category amounted to 53,914 "dan", worth 711,529 yuan, more than double that of fresh fish. In addition, various salted fish, refrigerated fish, and canned aquatic products totaled 1,008,337 "dan", worth 1,691,602 yuan. Furthermore, no Japanese fishing boats imported any catches in August.

### Cheng Xisheng Killed by Car 166

Died Unluckily While Coming to Shanghai to Raise Funds

Family Indignant, Filing a Lawsuit to Seek Justice

Cheng Xisheng, a prominent figure in the business community of Liyang, was elected as a representative to come to Shanghai to raise funds for disaster relief due to the severe floods in the county. After many days of meticulous contact, he was preparing to pack his bags and return home. One night (the 11th), at about 8 o'clock, he went out shopping with his companion, Di Shujing. While walking along Great World Avenue at the entrance of the China Department Store, a No. 737 car suddenly came speeding from behind, with its engine running at full power. Before they could avoid it, Cheng was knocked to the ground. Because the car was going too fast, it couldn't brake in time, causing the wheels to run over his legs and trap his long gown, crushing it in many places. Cheng's body was dragged several feet, resulting in a severe impact to his head and a fractured skull. He immediately lost consciousness. After the police arrived, they sent him to Renji Hospital for treatment, while taking the car, the owner, Mr. Lu, and the driver into custody for the time being. Cheng died in the hospital at 2 a.m. the next morning due to his severe injuries. Di, Cheng's companion, went to the police station to request severe punishment for the car in order to redress the wrong done to the deceased. The family of the deceased was extremely indignant and decided to consult with the Liyang native association in Shanghai and charitable organizations to hire a lawyer to file a lawsuit with the First Special District Court, seeking legal justice and redressing the wrong done to the deceased.

### Verdict in Abortion Resulting in Death Case 169

Wang Chen Sentenced to Three Years in Prison

Gao Dai Sentenced to One and a Half Years in Prison

A Yangzhou woman surnamed Yuan, residing at No. 1211 Wuzhou Road, became pregnant after having an affair. On August 18th, at 6 p.m., she asked Gao Dai, a woman from Jiangbei, to introduce Wang Chen, a fellow native, to her home to perform an abortion. She used a medicinal herb to insert into her lower body, resulting in injury and death. ### Assassination of Inspector, Two Killed by Gunfire 170

Those Who Helped "Little Changzhou" All Imprisoned for One Year

On August 20th, at around 6 a.m., Zhao Xilin, an inspector from the Shenxin No. 9 Yarn Factory in Yangshupu, was shot and wounded by "Little Changzhou" and others who were on the run at the factory gate. Stray bullets hit Zhang Wenjin and Li Liantang, killing them. Subsequently, Chinese and foreign detectives from the Yangshupu Police Station arrested the perpetrators: Qian Afu from Wuxi, Qiang Ruxing, Yan Jinlong from Yangzhou, and Han Cao, a Changzhou woman (the lover of "Little Changzhou"). They were handed over to the First Special District Court. It was learned during interrogation that, except for Qian Afu, all of them had helped "Little Changzhou" by borrowing silver dollars and pawning clothes to obtain money for his escape to other places. They were not present at the scene of the crime at the time. After the interrogation was concluded, awaiting sentencing. Yesterday morning, Judge Xiao Xiexun presided over the Third Criminal Court and sentenced Qiang Ruxing, Yan Jinlong, and Han Cao to one year of imprisonment each. The number of days of detention before the final judgment was commuted at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. Qian Afu was acquitted and released.

Reader Correspondence

### Inquiry from Qu Juejun 172

I joined the army ten years ago and have served as a secretary and other positions. I have also received considerable military training, led soldiers, and fought in battles. My monthly salary is not meager. Unfortunately, the environment is not good, and I always spend everything I earn. Therefore, I often feel that this kind of life is not suitable for my proper profession, and it is not guaranteed at all. Once the director is dismissed or transferred, I become panicked about losing my job. Even if I work twelve points hard and achieve outstanding results, I cannot withstand the current trends of deception and innovation. Moreover, at a time when natural and man-made disasters are occurring one after another, the country is not even a country, and there is even internal strife like "brothers fighting over beans." I really don't want to continue participating in such work of human mutual slaughter. Therefore, I have also made up my mind to change careers. Speaking of changing careers, how easy is it? I want to work, but I don't have the skills. I want to do business, but I don't have the capital. Besides, I can't find the right path. I have no choice but to express my aspirations first. I desperately want to find a proper and stable profession, no matter what it is, even if it's hard. I'm not afraid of that. I only need to be able to settle down and gradually make progress in business and knowledge with my own efforts and loyalty, without working in vain. This is the job that would satisfy me. As for my abilities, it can be said that I have no strengths. However, my physique is still strong, and I am not perfunctory in handling affairs. In my usual studies, I have some knowledge of English. I can translate ordinary books and newspapers, but I am not good at conversation. I also have some knowledge of Chinese official documents and letters. To what kind of industry can someone of my level change? I have translated a short piece in both Chinese and English and submit it for your perusal so that you can decide. Finally, I want to state that the stereotype that "a good man does not become a soldier" has not been fundamentally eradicated in the minds of the general public. If I change careers, I am afraid that others will know that I have worn a tiger's skin and will not dare to approach me. Even if they sympathize with me, they may even suspect that I have abandoned my existing military officer position and have other intentions. If I cause trouble as a result, that would be (wrongful and in vain). Another point is that my original hometown is Shaanxi. I followed my ancestors on official tours when I was young and took the official position as my home. I have not had a fixed residence. The vicissitudes of life have changed repeatedly, and my relatives and friends have withered away, leaving only me alone drifting in Zhejiang. I have been living here for more than twenty years and have not registered my residence. I am neither a native southerner nor a true northerner. Considering my life experience, I feel even more sorrow. Although it is said that under the flag of the blue sky and white sun, all ethnic groups are equal and local concepts should be eliminated, but customs have not changed, and I still feel inconvenienced. Moreover, my friends are all soldiers, and I have little contact with the outside world. I want to change careers, but I have no one to guide me. How can I solve this difficulty? I hope you can give me clear guidance.

(Reply) Your letter evokes deep sympathy and great admiration. I admire your determination to change careers because you do not want to continue participating in the work of human mutual slaughter. I agree with you. Unfortunately, this newspaper does not have a job placement office and I cannot know where there is a need for talent, so I cannot help you in practice. What I can say is that, according to your letter, you have a strong physique, are not perfunctory in handling affairs, and are willing to work hard and faithfully in your career. With these virtues, you will surely have a great development in the future, because these points can be said to be the (successful tickets). Moreover, the works you sent, both Chinese and English, have a considerable foundation, which is very difficult for you. According to your ability, from the perspective of being hired, you can be a clerk or secretary. I'm afraid that's quite enough. From the perspective of self-employment, you may want to try submitting articles to various daily, weekly, and monthly magazines. There may be considerable opportunities. Since you are still serving in the army, do not leave until you have secured a fixed position, so as not to fail.

Finally, I want to earnestly advise you not to be pessimistic, just keep fighting.

### Inquiry from a Certain Lady 173

I am a woman who has been harmed by my environment. I started school in Hankou Elementary School when I was seven years old. I graduated from elementary school when I was thirteen years old. Just when I wanted to enter middle school, a revolution broke out in Hankou, and warlords disturbed the peace. I came to Shanghai with my parents, and I have lost my education since then. How painful I felt at that time! Later, fortunately, a friend in Shanghai hired my father to Hangzhou to make a living, and the monthly income was only enough to cover expenses. As for my hope of pursuing my studies, it was gone. So I learned needlework to help with household expenses. After three years, my misfortune came. It was the summer of the 18th year of the Republic of China. My parents betrothed me. The other party was a college student. At that time, it was stated that I wanted to study. We got married in the spring of the following year. At first, our relationship was quite good, and he introduced me to a junior high school. Soon, I had a daughter. Because I was weak after giving birth, followed by a serious illness, he insisted on divorcing me and said, ("If you don't want to divorce, I will eventually harm you."). I am a weak woman, unable to make a living and unable to resist. Although we are currently living together, there is no affection at all. He looks at me with contempt all day long. I really have no way to think of it. I can only ask the master to point out a way to make a living for my poor, weak daughter. I am extremely grateful. If there is no limit to the length, please reply in your newspaper.

(Reply) After giving birth, love changes with appearance. It can be said that the other party is extremely inhuman. Thinking about it for you, there is room to advance and retreat, so there is no need to be pessimistic. First, you should guide the other party with a very sincere and very solemn attitude. You have relatives and friends in Shanghai, and you must have neighbors. You should move around and get to know more people, so that you can get more help when you need it. If it really doesn't work out, it's okay to let go. The other party said, ("If you don't want to divorce, I will eventually harm you.") I think it's a threat, and there won't be any facts. According to Article 1052 of the Civil Code, if one of the spouses intends to kill the other, he can request a divorce from the court. If the other party says this, it is evidence for you to request a divorce, and you can also request compensation and alimony in accordance with Articles 1056 and 1057. You said that when you were in your mother's house, you learned needlework to help with household expenses, so I think you still have the ability to be self-reliant, so you don't have to worry too much about the final disposition. However, we always hope that you two will reconcile.

Communication Stamp 175

Banquet for Chu Minyi by the National Arts Federation 176

Chu Talks About New Shortcuts to Xinjiang

The entire membership of the Shanghai National Arts Groups Federation and fifteen groups, including the Shanghai National Arts Museum, held a banquet yesterday at Jue Lin Public Hall for Chairman Chu Minyi. First, Weng Guozhu of the Wuxue Society stood up to give a speech, followed by Chu's reply. Chu said that he had long been determined to investigate the Northwest. Taking Beijing to Xinjiang as an example, in the past, it relied on the transport of vehicles and horses, which took more than 100 days to reach. Therefore, provinces such as Xinjiang were no less than uncivilized regions. All local products could only be transported out, and foreigners were able to restrict their selling prices. Economic oppression was at their mercy, which was helpless. It was more convenient to go through other countries than through one's own country. This time, with the use of scientific crawling vehicles, the journey has been reduced. From Beijing to Xinjiang, it now only takes more than thirty days. In the future, with some rectification and improvement of roads, etc., crawling vehicles will not even need this many days. Wouldn't this be of great benefit to national defense and people's livelihood? The new province is rich in special products and the people are simple and honest. However, there are many races, and it is not easy to integrate. Examining their physique and life, we Han people are far inferior. The Hui, Kazakh, and Mongol people are mostly strong and brave riders and have a resolute and brave temperament. The Han people have the habit of smoking opium and do not pay attention to physical education. Therefore, racial discrimination has a long history. The purpose of my trip is to open up the route to Xinjiang and to reconcile racial boundaries. In the new region, I wore their clothes and interacted with the locals. There was no separation between conversations and laughter. The national arts taichi exercises, taichi boxing, pushing hands, and equipment that I compiled were repeatedly performed in grand banquets and public groups in the area, with detailed demonstrations. The audience was large and warmly welcomed. Aspiring young people have completed the training in the shortest possible time and have requested the Provincial Department of Education to send them to Beijing to participate in the National Games. If this can be realized, wouldn't it be a happy event? At a time when natural and man-made disasters are imminent, it is important to carefully protect the miraculous effects of virtue and to enforce strict opium prohibition in the world that has already become a major concern.

At a time of internal and external troubles, all of us should work together to promote the popularization of national arts so that the people can exercise together. To seek a good foundation, taichi exercises are quite suitable because their movements are simple and interesting, suitable for both the elderly and the young. They are indeed not comparable to other sports. They will be published soon. Please give us your guidance. As for our Shanghai national arts colleagues, they have always been known for their reputation in previous examinations and competitions. I deeply hope that we can work together to ensure that we always maintain our achievements. Dozens of people at the banquet unanimously agreed and dispersed in joy.

People's Organizations Limited to Reorganize or Organize 177

Two Central Regulations

The Municipal Government Orders the Social Affairs Bureau to Comply

The Municipal Government has approved the Ministry of Industry's consultation and submission of two measures stipulated by the Central Government for people's organizations that have not fully complied with the regulations or have failed to reorganize or organize within the prescribed time limit. The Social Affairs Bureau has been ordered to comply with them and to instruct its subordinates to comply accordingly. The regulations are extracted below: (1) People's organizations that have reorganized or organized without fully complying with the central regulations on reorganization or organization will not be reorganized temporarily. However, the local party departments should order them to be reorganized separately in accordance with the law within one month before the expiration of the term of office of the officials of each people's organization, and then re-elect them to comply with the laws and regulations. (2) People's organizations that have failed to reorganize or organize within the time limit prescribed by the Central Government, except for the reorganization or organization of the Seafarers' Union and the Civil Ship Workers' Union, for which the Central Government has made separate provisions, must be reorganized or organized by October 1 of this year. Those who fail to do so will not be regarded as legal organizations.

Municipal Finance Bureau Stipulates Standard for Converting House Tax Silver to Yuan 178

Every Yuan is Equal to Seven Mace, Two Fen, and Five Li

To be Implemented Starting This Winter

The Municipal Finance Bureau issued a notice yesterday, stating, "In order to issue a notice, the Bureau's various collection offices collect house tax, which is based on the rent of the donors' houses, and issue tickets for collection by quarter, depending on whether the rent is calculated in silver or yuan. If the rent is calculated in silver, the house tax is also collected in silver. However, the price of silver fluctuates, and temporary conversion is quite cumbersome. In order to facilitate auditing and payment by the donors, the standard for converting silver is specifically stipulated. Starting this winter, all house taxes calculated in silver will be converted to one yuan at a rate of seven mace, two fen, and five li. From now on, the house tax for each quarter will be calculated according to the price set this time, regardless of the rise or fall in the price of silver. This has been submitted to the Municipal Government for approval and is now in the process of being implemented. In addition to ordering the Bureau's various collection offices to comply, this notice is hereby issued for public information."

Municipal Health Bureau Corrects the Production Method of Fushou Brand Pox Vaccine 182

The Municipal Health Bureau sent the director of the Health Testing Institute to inspect the Aikou Company Pox Vaccine Hall established by Japanese people on Hongqiao Road the other day. They saw that the production method of the Fushou brand pox vaccine they sell did not conform to the health principles. The cattle used for vaccination were not checked for tuberculosis, and the pox vaccine produced was not subjected to bacterial testing. They were hastily sold and applied, which was quite dangerous. All the houses and equipment were also extremely simple and did not meet the health standards. Special guidance was given and an order was issued to improve them, otherwise they would not be allowed to open. Although the Fushou brand pox vaccine was widely sold in the past due to its low price, it has now been found that the production method does not conform to the standards. Before the improvement is completed and approved by the bureau, it is hoped that hospitals and doctors will no longer use it in order to avoid harming the vaccinated people.

Ciyou Association Rescues Kong Sanbao 183

Kong Jingqing, who lives at No. 18, Xinhua Li, Tongfu Road, used to be a French businessman. He owned property, smoked opium, and had a concubine. His wife, Ying, was fierce and could not tolerate her. The concubine could not bear her abuse and fled, leaving behind a daughter named Sanbao, who was only four years old. Ying vented her anger on the girl, abusing her severely. The neighbors all felt injustice. Yesterday, she was beaten again. The girl's cheeks were bruised and purple, and she was covered in scars and could not stop crying. Chen Jusheng, a righteous person in the neighborhood, could not bear it and reported it to the China Ciyou Association. The association immediately sent a cadre from the protection department to the Jing'an Temple Police Station to investigate with Chinese and foreign detectives. Kong Jingqing was full of opium and skillfully evaded the investigation, claiming that he had hidden the girl outside. At first, he falsely claimed that her surname was Bao and refused the investigation. Later, when the investigators could not find the girl, Kong demanded compensation for damage to his reputation, and his momentum was fierce and unstoppable. However, when searching the hall and upstairs, they saw many opium utensils. The police pointed to his opium utensils and said, "We are here today to investigate child abuse and will not ask about your opium crime. If you continue to be cunning, we will first seize your opium utensils." Kong's anger was slightly reduced. Xu Ruizhang, the concierge, testified that Kong had asked the nanny to take the girl to the station early this morning to take the express train to Hangzhou. When she left the neighborhood, she saw that the girl's cheeks were bruised and purple, and her hands and feet were injured. Chen's male servant also gave the same testimony. Kong's chauffeur also provided detailed testimony to confirm it. Kong did not dare to argue strongly and confessed that the girl had been abused by his wife, Ying, and he could not bear her pain, so he sent her to Hangzhou for recuperation. The association and the police thought that since he had confessed, they ordered him to hand over the girl and would not arrest him for the time being. Later, lawyer Wu Linkun went to the police station to take responsibility for handing over the girl within a week and was willing to thoroughly protect the girl, designating a kindergarten near the Jing'an Temple Police Station as a place for education and asked the Ciyou Association to take care of her at any time and the police to visit her from time to time to ensure her safety. As for Kong, who violated humanity, I don't know if the police have taken any action to deal with him.

Holding a Harmonica Music Concert

And Adding a Special Elementary Class

Since the opening of classes this month by the China Harmonica Society, organized by harmonica expert Mr. Wang Qingxun, registrations have continued to pour in. FREE TALK

NOT REMOVING GARDEN GRASS STUDIO - Casual Talks

THE COST OF A BOWL OF NOODLES 197

One afternoon last year, I went to the New Allen Cinema hungry and took advantage of the ten-minute intermission to go to the entrance and eat a bowl of noodles. This bowl of noodles cost fourteen copper coins, and it only took five minutes to cook and eat, which was extremely economical. Seeing that there were still five minutes, I took the opportunity to ask about the noodle stall's business situation. The vendor's surname was Shen. The entire set of equipment was worth eighteen yuan, the cost of materials was two yuan, and the monthly donation to the police station was two yuan. He could earn thirty yuan a month. I said that your income is a little better than a village teacher. He said it was hard work, going home at four o'clock every night and getting up at seven o'clock in the morning to buy materials to prepare the noodles and dumplings for the day. If he didn't do this, his family wouldn't be able to live. I saw that Mr. Shen's face was yellow and thin, and it was indeed the result of too much hard work. A bowl of noodles for fourteen copper coins, although a commoner's lunch, is exchanged for the health of another commoner. Thinking about this this year, I was filled with emotion and wrote a poem to send to old Shen, but old Shen has disappeared.

(A bowl of noodles in front of the New Allen gate, costs fourteen small copper coins. The vendor's name is Old Shen, acting as both worker and boss. He can earn thirty yuan a month, better than a teacher running a noodle stall. Who knows, he says (It's hard work, only sleeping three hours a night, if I sleep a moment longer, who will feed my freezing and starving children?) Looking at him from head to toe; a withered tree standing in the autumn wind. I know the cost of the noodles, it's not copper, it's blood!)

FRAGMENTS OF THE CAPITAL 198

—Cockscomb

The capital's flood has not yet receded. Xingzhongmen Outer Street is the only way to enter the city from Xiaguan. Previously, the Municipal Works Bureau built a plank bridge at the flooded area to facilitate passage, with sandbags blocking both sides of the bridge. Police officers stood there holding red and green flags to direct vehicles, which was quite special. However, the number of vehicles in the capital has been increasing day by day. In addition to public buses, there are official vehicles from various agencies, unlicensed taxis operating on the streets, as well as horse-drawn carriages and rickshaws. In the past, those entering the city could pass through Yijiangmen, but now they all pass through this road, often causing congestion and making it difficult to pass. Those sitting in the car can often hear the shouts and arguments of the drivers.

People sympathize with disaster relief. Most of the disaster victims in the capital live in makeshift shelters made of reed mats on high ground in the city. Others, such as the platform at Xiaguan Railway Station, also have many refugees sitting and lying there, surviving on just a few steamed buns each day. Since the citizens launched a disaster relief campaign, all parties have enthusiastically donated, greatly benefiting the disaster victims. Currently, various entertainment venues are holding fundraising events. The World and National Cinemas have added a movie screening at 10:00 AM every day, with all ticket revenue going to disaster relief. This is indeed a first. The streets of Xiaguan are flooded, and several small schools are trapped by the water. The start of the semester is approaching, but the students are waiting and watching. However, they cannot be allowed to drop out of school. Therefore, wooden planks are laid in front of the school gates, shaped like gangplanks used when ships dock. The students' families take great care of their children and send servants to accompany them morning and evening. It is heard that in several small schools, classes are still affected by the water. There are not enough classrooms, so the remedy is that students of all grades take turns attending classes in the morning and afternoon, so that they can rest for half a day each day.

WORLD TIDBITS 199

Fashion from Seven Thousand Years Ago. Selim Hassan, the famous Egyptian archaeologist, recently excavated the tomb of the ancient Egyptian King Tarso Ankh. He was a prince and the third dynasty's bishop, who ruled Egypt seven thousand years ago. He was well-known. The tomb contains statues of the king and statues of his wife and two daughters. The two daughters are all wearing sky-blue clothes, short collars, open chests, and short skirts that reach just above the knees. Their necks are adorned with jewelry. This is not much different from modern women's clothing.

▲Long-Distance Motorcycle Trip. In the autumn of 1929, an engineer from Bradford, England, and a young man from London, both with adventurous spirits, suddenly had a grand idea one day. They rode a motorcycle from London to Sydney in New South Wales. In March 1930, they arrived in Canberra and soon reached the end point, covering a distance of 17,000 miles. Such a trip is truly not an easy feat. (Sea Guest)

UNHEARD-OF DANCE COMPETITION 200

—Ming

The dance competition held in Paris, France, has caused a global sensation. On the morning of July 22, two French girls danced continuously for 752 hours, about 31 days, setting a new record for long-term dancing, and won a prize of 100 pounds.

When the dance competition opened, the contestants were all young men and women who were usually good at dancing. The competition used the length of time as the standard for winning. Initially, all the dance partners were able to dance day and night without interruption. However, as the days went on, the weaker ones couldn't hold on and left the arena one after another, giving up the championship. In the end, only this winning couple remained. At 4:00 AM on July 22, they also fell to the ground from exhaustion.

Suddenly, the female partner, Xiao Su, whispered, (I can't dance anymore.) But counting the days, it had already reached 752 hours. The others had already left. Moreover, another dance partner suddenly stopped dancing the day before because the female partner injured her foot. Otherwise, they would have been formidable rivals. It was impossible to predict who would win.

During the dance competition, the consumption of shoes by this pair of dance partners was unprecedented. In these 31 days, the female partner wore out 20 pairs of shoes, and the male partner wore out 8 pairs. As a result of the competition, the second prize went to the dance partner who stopped the day before, with a difference of only half a day. It was both fortunate and unfortunate.

The competition held in Paris was quite successful. As a result, the organizers plan to hold another one in London in the near future, with a prize of as much as 1,600 pounds. As for the competition method, participants can only stop for 15 minutes every hour. The remaining time must be spent dancing continuously day and night. The couple with the longest time without interruption will win the championship.

NEW SOUNDS IN THE SPRING COLOURS OF THE SINGING STAGE 201

— Sheng Han

The last days of summer have arrived, and the heat is receding. The evening breeze is cool, and the mind feels more refreshed. Suddenly, I received a call from Drunkard Weng, saying that the newly filmed (Spring Colours of the Singing Stage) would be screened informally at the Guanglu Cinema, inviting me to watch it. I happily hired a car and went. When I arrived, the screening was about to begin. After taking my seat for a moment, I heard the sound of music coming from the screen. It was the overture performed by the music troupe led by the famous musician Henry Natnan. The softness and clarity of the light and the accuracy and clarity of the sound are indeed no different from the best imported films. The whole play begins and ends with singing, which is very intriguing. The first song is (The Joy of Youth), with lyrics and music by Li Jinhui. The lyrics are: (1) The spring light is beautiful, the spring colour is charming, the spring feeling is deep, the spring heart is quiet. The pear blossom face is too enchanting, the apricot eyes contain affection, and the peach looks are with smiles. The green is curved, the willow eyebrows are long, and the red is beautiful. The cherry is small. The spring sun is warm, and the spring clouds are vast. Dance in the spring breeze. The willow waist is slender, the fresh flowers are blooming, and the tender stamens contain buds. Don't let down the arrival of the new spring. (2) The spring light is beautiful, the spring colour is charming, the spring feeling is deep, the spring heart is quiet. Open the curtains and arrange the sheng and xiao. The good couple comes together, and good friends arrive together. Love is continuous, like two fish side by side. Love is earnest, like two birds living together. The melody is melodious, and the singing is beautiful. Dance lightly, embracing each other. The love flower is blooming, and the love stamens contain buds. Don't let down the youth. (Finale) The new spring colour, the good spring light, take advantage of the youth, enter the joy. Plant the seeds of love. Love will be eternal and affection will be long. Open the flowers of joy. Joy will be boundless. Bear the fruit of happiness. Happiness will be boundless. Good friends are paired. Lovers are together. Don't let down the passionate singing. The last song is (Kapok Wind), with lyrics by Gao Tianqi and music by Qiu Qixiang. The lyrics are: 1. The afterglow flies in the sky. The setting sun is faint and sleepy. How can you bear to see the good scenery go by in a hurry? The intimate feelings are both vast and tender. Spring goes, dreams like smoke. The heartbroken person stands in the evening breeze. 2. The butterflies flutter. The fallen flowers are red and pitiful. The willow silk does not tie the spring light. Rain is bitter, and the wind is sour for another year. Two swallows talk in front of the curtain. New sorrows and old hatreds are all intertwined.

THE AMERICAN FILM INDUSTRY (II) 202

—Ji Ping

The American film industry is really in a slump right now. The lower and middle classes are struggling with the bread and butter issue, and there seems to be no way to solve it. People who have always been addicted to movies are now oppressed by economic forces and have no interest in going to the movies. According to the reports of major theaters, the average number of viewers has decreased by more than 30% in the past year. Many theaters have closed down due to declining business. The sales of films produced by film companies have also been greatly affected. When I (Hong's self-reference) was in Hollywood, in addition to the three major companies, Fox, R.K.O., and Paramount, several others reduced production and barely maintained, while several others were already in a state of stagnation.

In the past, when the film industry was booming, film companies often spent hundreds of thousands or even millions of dollars on shooting a film. The salaries of star directors were so generous that they were truly shocking. Now that the film industry has declined, all companies are adopting a tightening policy and laying off actors on a large scale. As a result, many people have lost their jobs. If a film is to be shot, the director must first make a precise budget, which must be approved by the company before it can be implemented. It is not like before, when funds could be used without limitation. There are also companies that sign contracts with directors to buy their independently produced films. The adoption of this contracting system is nothing more than an expedient measure to save expenses and reduce costs.

Two big stars in Hollywood have recently had stories. One is director Ernst Lubitsch, and the other is female star Clara Bow. They are both resentful and negative because of (love), to the point of sacrifice. Ernst Lubitsch is willing to work hard to study film art, so his directed productions are popular all over the world and his name is famous for a time. He had a friend, a screenwriter whom he had promoted to fame, who had an ambiguous relationship with Lubitsch's wife. Lubitsch was greatly stimulated by this and his mood deteriorated, which affected his work. The content of his new film (The Smiling Lieutenant) is not as good as before. From this, we can see the importance of psychological state and life relationship. Clara Bow is one of Hollywood's biggest stars. Recently, she was blackmailed by a tabloid that failed and defamed her, resulting in losses in both reputation and status. The editor of the tabloid has recently been arrested and imprisoned for eight years. Although she won the lawsuit, she is afraid that she will retire from now on.

In recent years, major theaters in the United States have had many new facilities, such as (1) Another stage is set up at the entrance of the theater to perform miscellaneous operas, so that the audience who have already bought tickets and are waiting at the entrance will not feel lonely. (2) A room is set up to store children, and female nurses are hired to take care of them. Many women like to bring their children to the theater, but sometimes they cry and laugh, which disrupts the order and causes opposition from the audience. Their facility is like a temporary kindergarten, which is convenient for women and audiences. The method of storing children there is the same as storing clothes and hats in restaurants and dance halls. A number is also taken, and when picking them up, just give the number to the nurse, match the number, and the child will be picked up. I think that major theaters at sea can follow this example. The cost is limited, but the effect is great. Why not do it?

Narratives of the Rotary Club

A HUSBAND'S WIFE (XIV) 203

— Jiang Hongjiao

Mr. Li's emotions were really like a torrent. At first, he just thought that if he had someone like Mrs. Chen to accompany him to see movies and go to dance halls, his life could be a lot richer. His own wife was far less beautiful and generous than Mrs. Chen. Having a woman like Mrs. Chen running around with him was like a very honourable thing; he achieved this goal, so he planned how to further express himself to Mrs. Chen. Once, sitting together watching a movie, he leaned his body closer to her, secretly observing whether she would refuse or sit away in the opposite direction? But she seemed not to notice, and remained still. His heart was pounding, almost to the point where he could hear the sound of his heart beating. He secretly used all his strength in the dark and slightly bright light to focus on her eyelashes, to focus on her expression, and felt that they were beautiful and kind. She coughed slightly by chance, and he asked her very gently and lowly: (Are you a little cold)? As he said that, he reached out to hold her hand. He had held her hand very generously—or rather, very tolerantly—in front of Mr. Chen before. Now, this handshake position was not special at all, but the psychological composition was completely different. The passionate emotions seemed to pass like electricity to his fingertips, and contact with her warm and soft palm seemed to cause sparks.

She quickly turned her head towards him with a shallow smile, (Oh)? This sound seemed to pretend not to understand, and seemed to indicate acceptance of this electric conduction. It was very charming and gentle, arousing—perhaps enticing—him to have the opportunity to say a second sentence.

(You're coughing, are you cold?) Seeing that she didn't refuse, he held her hand tighter.

(No. Your hand is cold.)

He pretended to loosen her hand, wanting to retract his own hand. But she held his hand tightly and didn't let go.

(Your hand will get cold too.)

(No, I'll warm it for you.) She simply covered his hand with her other hand. He fully understood her emotions, which were also firing at the other party, just like two ships in the ocean, each approaching the other, echoing each other and sending wireless signals to each other, so he planned to make a further expression.

COMMERCIAL NEWS

Financial Gold Price Trends Upward Again 204

▲ Gold Rises Seven Taels, Six Mace: Yesterday, the 14th, the standard gold price once again soared, moving swiftly. The difference between the highest and lowest price of the day was only two or three taels, with an overall market spread of about ten taels. Buyers were excited. It was said that the sellers believed the settlement date was approaching, fearing they would have to pay a premium, so they vigorously resisted, appearing quite panicked. The final result was a rise of almost ten taels. Initially, the market was relatively flat, with the silver bars slightly declining compared to the previous day. Later, foreign exchange showed explicit easing but implicit tightening. With buyers being particularly strong, prices rose sharply, breaking through the 770 tael mark. Subsequently, the market stabilized, fluctuating by only two or three taels. Drafts contracted by half a point. Market confidence was strong, with expectations of 72 taels or more. It was rumored that the large bars might fall this morning.

▲ Morning Close Sees Vigorous Growth: The October opening price this morning rose slightly by six candareens, reaching 763 taels and 7 mace. The large bar silver for forward delivery only fell by one-sixteenth. The current spot price of silver remained unchanged. US stocks declined by just over four dollars. In the market, Zhi Feng Yong, Da De Cheng, Ri Chang, and others all advanced, continuing from 63 taels and 5 mace to 7 taels and 5 mace. Later, because Yuan Mao Yong, Yong Feng, Fu Shun, and others were privy to HSBC's impending increase in posted rates, they retreated to 4 taels and 2 mace. In an instant, Da De Cheng, Fu Yu, Sen Chang Yong, Tong Tai Chang, and others came to purchase, raising the price by 4 taels. Nearly all British gold firms were settling for December at 1.25, and had increased to 8 taels and 45 mace. When the British gold announcement indeed showed an increase of 1.25, US gold by 0.25, and Japanese gold a decrease of 1.5 fen, it immediately retreated to 7 taels and 5 mace. Heng Yu Yuan Cheng Yong and others sold, at which time the price fell from 68 taels to 6 taels. Internal markets were flat. October still settled at 1.25. After 10 o'clock, Yuan Xing Yong, Ri Chang, Yu Da, Qian Chang Xiang, Tong Tai Chang, Fu Chang Bing Xing, and others all advanced, selling British gold at 1.25, causing the gold price to surge by 4 taels, fluctuating by only a few candareens to one tael. Soon after, it exceeded 70 taels, reaching 70 taels and 0.3 mace by 11:30. At this time, Sumitomo sold December British gold at 1.25, and with Heng Xing Da De Cheng and others also selling, it immediately retreated to 69 taels and 3 mace. Subsequently, British gold remained firm, with October settling at only 0.0625. Zhi Feng Yong Yuan Cheng Chun Yuan Yong Bing Xing Yong Feng Hong Xing and others were all vying to purchase, instantly rising 4 taels. Indian exchange rates showed small short-term gains and larger long-term gains, but not exceeding one anna. At noon, it reached 73 taels and a half, then closed at 3 taels, with the posted price revised to 783 taels, a decrease of 15 to 10 taels.

▲ Post-Market Consolidation: The post-market opened at 73 taels and 1 mace, then 3 taels and 9 mace. Indian exchange fell slightly by one anna, but with Bing Xing Yuan Xing Yong selling, it retreated to 2 taels and 8 mace. Later, Yuan Mao Yong Da De Cheng and others bought in, and Mitsui also purchased October British gold at 3 pence, further shrinking British gold by 0.125, US gold by 0.25, and Japanese gold increasing by 1.5 fen, reaching 73 taels and 5 mace by 2:30. Subsequently, HSBC offered November British gold at 3 pence, but Tong Tai Chang continued to sell, so it fell slightly by 2 taels. At 3:30, it was 70 taels and 0.7 mace. Suddenly, it was heard that Indian exchange had fallen slightly by one anna, and was being dragged in by arbitrage, reaching 2 taels and a half at 4:00. Afterwards, it fluctuated slightly by one tael, reaching 1 tael and 6 mace at one point. The market closed at 4:30 at 72 taels and 7 mace, an increase of 9 taels and 6 mace compared to last Saturday. The highest price for the entire day was 73 taels and 9 mace, and the lowest was 63 taels and 5 mace, a difference of 10 taels and 4 mace.

▲ Spot Red Transactions Flat: The spot price in the early market was 60 taels and 8 mace, the noon close was 73 taels, the afternoon was 3 taels and 3 mace, and the closing price was 3 taels. The initial posted price decrease was around 10 taels, later revised to 790 taels and 0.2 mace, a decrease of 17 to over 19 taels, and finally over 17 taels. Recorded prices were 70 taels and 72 taels, with the premium before and after the market remaining at 70 taels. Spot red bars were flat. The firm Yíng Fēng Héng Tóng Fēng Yǒng sold several hundred taels to the guest trading houses at a price increasing by 7 taels and 7 mace and 5 candareens.

▲ Buyers Predominate in Transactions: According to statistics, Cheng Feng Yong, Yuan Xing Yong, Fu Yu, Fu Chang, Yuan Kang Xiang, Tong Tai Chang, Wan Xing, Cui Chang Yong, Zhi Feng Yong, Bing Xing, Sen Chang Yong, and Chun Yuan Yong all bought in. Da De Cheng, Shun Li, Qian Chang Xiang, and Fu Tai Heng sold more than they bought. Yuan Mao Yong's buying and selling were balanced, still selling over 400 bars. Heng Xing also sold over 200 bars. Yi Feng Yong, Yuan Tai, Yong Feng, Yuan Heng, Da Xing Yong, and Yuan Chun had occasional transactions. Speculator Wu bought and sold. In the afternoon, Da De Cheng, Heng Xing, Yuan Sheng Yuan Heng, and Yuan Tai all bought in. As for the physical bars, Shun Li, Tong Tai Chang, Yuan Xing Yong, Bing Xing, Zhi Feng Yong, Qian Chang Xiang, and Fu Chang all sold. The Cantonese traders bought in after selling earlier, for a total of just over 500 bars. Including non-Cantonese traders, the buying and selling were similar, for a total of 1500-1600 bars. Because arbitrage was not favorable, there were no large-scale transactions.

The rest all followed suit. However, the Hong Kong rate decreased slightly by 0.1875, calculated at 79 taels and 9.375 mace. All other rates also decreased, except for the Hong Kong rate, which remained unchanged. As for the trend in the domestic market, it was tightened. It was firm from the morning and then became even stronger. The post-market showed a steady state. Compared to last Saturday, the British gold decreased by 0.1875, the US dollar by 0.375, and the Japanese gold increased by 1.5 fen. The gold market had already broken through the 70 tael mark. This was due to the settlement date approaching, forcing those with short positions to quickly cover. Chinese merchants engaged in settlement again. There were some sales in the afternoon. It is estimated that a total of over 200,000 pounds of British gold were traded, and only a small amount of US dollars changed hands. Silver Dollar Market Appears Calm 207

▲ Market Conditions: Trading in the market yesterday was still not very active. Compared to last Monday, there was a significant difference. Currently, the financial community is concerned about the massive losses from the recent Han River disaster, the stockpiling of goods, and the impact on businesses, inevitably leading to financial strain. Therefore, although the exterior appears calm, there are genuine hidden worries. The current tightness of the silver supply is likely the cause.

▲ Premium/Discount Prices: (Silver Premium) The early market premium was 7 candareens, 2 fen, 4 li, 7 hao, and a half, which was equivalent to the early market of the previous day. The noon market was slightly smaller by 1 hao and 2 hu and a half, at 7 candareens, 2 fen, 4 li, 6 hao, and 2 hu and a half. (Silver Discount) The early market was 1 candareen and 7 fen, the noon market was 1 candareen and 4 fen, slightly smaller by 4-5 fen compared to the previous day. The premium for additional water was 8-9 fen. Bank rates were 7 fen, the situation remained strong, and it is feared that it will not ease easily in the short term.

▲ Subsidiary Coin Market: Jiangnan small dollars were the same in both the early and noon markets at 6 candareens and 6 fen, a decrease of 2 li compared to the early market of the previous day. 4,000 jiao were traded in the early market, and 4,500 jiao in the noon market. Guangdong small dollars were 6 candareens and 5 fen and 2 li in the early market, and 6 candareens and 5 fen and 2 li, 1 hao, and 2 hu and a half in the noon market. 125,000 jiao were traded in the early market, and 35,000 jiao in the noon market. Copper coins were reduced by 500 wen, to 372,000 wen.

▲ Silver Dollar Inflow and Outflow: (Silver Amounts) Yesterday, Monday, the banks opened, so there were slightly more receipts and deliveries. Chinese banks received and delivered 2.7-2.8 million in drafts, foreign banks received and delivered over 2.9 million in drafts, special amounts received and delivered 2-3 million, and various goods, taxes, and miscellaneous amounts received and delivered 9.8-9.9 million. 500,000 went into storage and 400,000 came out of storage. Japanese banks received and delivered various amounts of over 3.9 million, special amounts of 600,000-700,000, and 300,000 came out of storage. Money shops and silver firms received and delivered over 49 million in single orders, and over 4.3 million in overdraft amounts. 1.4 million in remittance amounts were received and delivered, and 200,000-300,000 were received in cash. (Foreign Currency Amounts) In the early market, 1.465 million in remittance drafts were transacted, and 1.37 million in the noon market. 75,000 in banknotes were transacted in the early market, and 40,000 in the noon market, plus 30,000 in check orders. In the off-exchange banknote market, 190,000 was transacted in the early market, and 135,000 in the noon market. In bank trading, interbank trading was 600,000 in the early market, and 450,000 in the noon market. The inflow and outflow of foreign accounts among banks was over 1.8 million, with banknote inflows and outflows of over 3 million. Money shops received and delivered over 7.8 million in foreign single orders, and over 2.2 million in foreign overdraft amounts. The trading volume of small money shops was 600,000-700,000.

Cotton Yarn and Cotton Prices Stabilize 209

The yarn market has stabilized, but the situation for imported cotton yarn is not good, trending downwards. Local sentiment is still good because there are fewer new sellers, and the exchange floor is tight. However, Japanese merchants are selling from time to time, and the actual sales volume in the market is still small. Sporadic transactions continue. Currently, most are in short positions, due to the severe floods in all directions, which may impact future demand.

▲ Near-Month Man-Marked Yarn Trending Upwards: The man-marked yarn market opened in the early market with fewer sellers. Although imported cotton was down slightly, market sentiment remained firm, with each month rising by 2-3 mace. The market opened firmly in the afternoon, but two or three varieties trended downwards and market conditions weakened again, with near months rising by 1-2-3 mace and far months falling by 1-2-3 mace. A total of 11,600 bales were traded. Public Tai sold 1,300 bales, Rui Da 700 bales, Yi Yu 2,400 bales, Geng Feng 1,050 bales, and Tian Long 600 bales. Hou Feng Chang bought 1,050 bales, Tong Yu 2,250 bales, De Ji 950 bales, and Chang Feng 750 bales. The closing prices are listed below:

Cotton Market Dull and Unremarkable 210

The cotton market is extremely dull, as the American cotton market is weak, trending downwards, leading to poor sentiment. However, the local weather is not good, and new sellers are cautious, so the exchange floor remains tight. Market prices cannot fall accordingly. Japanese merchants and speculators, viewing the unstable global situation, are unanimously selling short. Domestic cotton merchants, considering the severe floods in all directions and the poor production, are uniquely taking long positions.

▲ Lack of Sellers in the Hankou-Marked Cotton Market: The Hankou-marked cotton exchange opened in the early market with tight sentiment due to the lack of sellers. As a result, the current month rose by 2 mace and the far month was flat. The market remained tight after opening in the afternoon, but the second round fell back, resulting in a flat outcome. The total trading volume for the entire day was 40,500 dan. Mei Ji sold 2,500 dan, Yuan Da 2,300 dan, Geng Feng 2,200 dan, Yi Yu 2,300 dan, Tai Xing 1,100 dan, and Tian Long 1,800 dan. Ji Feng bought 4,500 dan, Xin Cheng 1,800 dan, Chang He 1,300 dan, Public Tai 1,000 dan, Tong Yu 1,900 dan, and Chang Feng 1,300 dan. The closing prices are listed below:
