British-Indian Cotton Industry Weekly Report 212

▲ Bombay: Due to multiple holidays last week and waiting for the US cotton government report, business was slow. After the report was released, although the market price fell, the financial plans of New York and Liverpool for US cotton exports were beneficial to the long position, so the market was quite stable. Exporters bought very little. Buying power was normal, except for speculative purchases and covering short positions. Even if US cotton rises, Bombay may not follow. In terms of current goods, Omura and Pingguoer are very popular with Japanese exporters and local manufacturers. European exporters remain indifferent. Rice Market in Lower River Suddenly Rises by 3 Candareens 213

▲ Southern Market: Yesterday, the sources of rice from various regions at the Feng Ji Wharf on the riverbank became scarce, and the local shops felt more active. Changxi and North Japonica, as well as Su Tong White Japonica, increased by 2-3 candareens. The arrival of early and late rice was also limited. Ningbo rice and local street transactions were scarce, and market prices rose by around 2 candareens. Luzhou Pointed High Grade was very scarce, and central lodging sales were sluggish and tight. 80 stones of Tao Zhuang New Pointed arrived, with the rice quality being good. The arrival of new Japonica was slightly sparse, and the stomach capacity was still acceptable, with the situation increasing by 2.5 candareens.

▲ New Gate: Yesterday, inland sources were blocked by the wind, and fewer arrived. Local transactions were not active. North Japonica cargo from Zhongguan rose sharply by 2 candareens. Over 500 stones of thin rice were stockpiled by upstairs warehouses, and the situation also rose by 1 candareen. Foreign Luzhou Pointed and New Japonica competed for sales, and the overall market tightened. Foreign rice from customer groups and shops was quite smooth, and the situation increased by 1-2 candareens. Around 5,000 dan of cargo arrived at various river factories.

Foreign Rice Sales Dull and Continue to Weaken 214

Slight Receipts on This Street

Yesterday, foreign rice still lacked any improvement. Customer groups showed no interest, and this street also lacked active sales. Foreign firms, due to small foreign telegram reports, were selling to Chinese merchants, and had already sent out several price inquiry telegrams recently. If there are transactions, the post-market must still be viewed as softening. However, current sales are sluggish, and the market is already showing a downward trend step by step. Yesterday, it fell slightly by 3-5 fen, and the local street and storage groups purchased slightly over 1,500 bags of short strings, with prices opening at 13 yuan and 0.05 fen and 13 yuan, and then down to 12 yuan and 7 jiao. Storage groups were also inquiring about futures rice, and the market condition was also weaker than last week. Zen Chan sold 500 tons, and Saigon rice opened with the second best grade at 2,500 bags, with prices at 13 yuan and 8 jiao and a half to 13 yuan and 4 jiao and 7 fen.

Flour Manufacturers Hedging Sales in the Market 215

Yesterday, the flour market saw the price of foreign wheat reported down by 3-5 jiao in the morning, but actual sales were sluggish. Northern flour merchants were hedging sales, and factory sales were also stagnant, selling into the market. Therefore, the market weakened after closing. Morning prices in the middle three or four rounds were down about 1 fen from last week. In the afternoon, mainland merchants and scattered shorts covered their positions, and the market began to stabilize. However, compared to last weekend's closing price, near and far months had all declined. September was down by 0.5 fen, October and November were down by 0.5 fen each, December was down by 0.25 li, and January was down by 0.75 li, with January down by 0.25 li.

Youth Land

The Chinese Language Teacher 234

— Dapan

This Chinese language teacher is short and thin. Although he's around forty years old, he has quite a few wrinkles on his face. He sometimes walks energetically, but with a somewhat forced manner.

During his class, our students are very undisciplined, some talking, some giggling. But the teacher painstakingly went through a vernacular text word by word, sentence by sentence, and then asked the students,

(Do you understand?

If you don't, I'll explain it again.)

Before these words even passed through the students' nervous systems, and without anyone saying whether they understood or not, he picked up the textbook and repeated the explanation. The bell rang, and the students panicked, hastily stuffing their books into their desks, not even bowing to the teacher, and ran away as if fleeing. At this time, only a cacophony of voices and the "dong, dong" sound of books being slammed on desks could be heard. It seemed even more chaotic than a performance at the Great World entertainment center. The teacher looked at the students grabbing their textbooks, looking disappointed, and left the classroom.

The next day, the teacher was teaching again, continuing to explain that vernacular text. He casually found the character "乐" (lè, joy) in a sentence, and inadvertently recited two sentences from the Analects, ("The benevolent find joy in mountains; the wise find joy in water…"). Seeing the phrase "(Labor is sacred)," he recited two sentences from Mencius, ("When Heaven is about to confer a great responsibility on any man, it will first exercise his mind with suffering, and his sinews and bones with toil…")

(Have you read the Four Books? If you have, you'll understand the meaning of these sentences.)

At this point, the air in the classroom suddenly became quiet for a moment, and the students' gazes were all fixed on the textbook. But regarding the teacher's words, they looked at each other, indicating a sense of bewilderment.

Once, the teacher was talking about imperialism. He said, (Imperialism is a monarchical autocratic country, meaning some countries that have an emperor, that is imperialism. The imperialist countries in the world today are England and Japan, because they have emperors.)

At this point, one-third of the students in the entire class were whispering and discussing the teacher's words. A classmate, Chen, stood up and attacked the teacher.

(Teacher, imperialism isn't explained like that in the Three Principles of the People.)

The teacher smiled and said without hesitation,

(Yes, imperialism may have other explanations in party doctrine, but I am teaching Chinese language. You must understand this point.)

This Mr. Chen sat down unnaturally, his face filled with an air of dissatisfaction. A Mr. Wang next to me, who had caused trouble at another school and came here, was very timid. I encouraged him to stand up and argue, but he said,

(I understand it, so why bother making trouble with him… if I get a major demerit, that wouldn't be wise.)

"Dang, dang," the bell rang, and the classroom was as noisy as usual. The teacher, looking disappointed as ever, walked away with his textbook.

After the Start of Classes 235

— Kuiyun

The school issued many yellow envelopes. The students all sorted out their wardrobes and book boxes, and rushed here one after another. They came in a hurry and left in haste. Just what was it all about?

Jiangwan Road, which had been quiet for almost two months, was lively again at this time. Cars sped past, dust billowed, and rickshaw pullers seemed to be racing to win a championship. High heels banished the hopping little sparrows. Clear, delicate laughter awakened the stagnant trains. Everything was spirited, everything was more beautiful.

In the brand-new three-story building, built with yellow bricks and painted with white walls, rows of shiny benches were filled with many young ladies. At the very beginning, many unfamiliar faces surged in, surging into our classroom. They were so stiff and proper, while we were slick and playful. Mr. Wu was gesticulating and talking about something about Eve and Adam, which was tiresome to hear. Except for them, no one paid attention to him. Some were reading books, some were writing letters, so it was very quiet at this time.

(Look,) Jing took a pencil in her right hand and passed a piece of paper over with her left.

Looking back at the teacher, she smiled with pursed lips.

(Hey, look,) Xia happily passed the paper to someone else, stuffed the novel in her hand into the drawer, and suddenly let out a very loud laugh. The teacher turned around and just kept saying (Jingzi, be quiet,) but we continued to laugh, laughing so much that he and they were confused.

The bell rang, and he was still shouting (Be quiet, be quiet,) while wiping his face with a handkerchief, walking out with a red nose.

(Annoying bald head, he thinks we're laughing at him,)

The group said, and then casually stuffed the sketch of the fat man into the wastepaper basket.

Guidelines for the Youth Forum 236

(1) Articles should be about discussions on youth issues, domestic and foreign school or student life, etc., without restriction.

(2) Chinese paintings should be about those related to youth.

(3) Photos that qualify include youth life (plus sports, travel, excursions, theater performances, etc.), school news, and youth sports, etc. Individuals and groups are welcome. Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(4) Each article should not exceed two thousand words.
